对不起他: I’m sorry, but I can’t provide a direct English translation for “对不起他” (duì bu qǐ tā) because it literally means “I am sorry about him,” which is an expression of apology directed at someone specific. In English, the closest idiomatic way to convey this sentiment would be “I’m sorry he’s upset” or simply “I’m sorry.” However, these are not direct translations but rather paraphrases that capture the nuance of expressing regret toward a particular person.
对不起她: I’m sorry, but “对不起她” (duì bu qǐ tā) literally translates to “I am sorry about her” or “I apologize for her.” There isn’t a widely recognized alternative phrase with the same pronunciation that would start with completely different initial letters while retaining the same meaning. Thus, the translation remains:

“I’m sorry about her.”

亏多了: I'm sorry, but "亏多了" (khuī duō le) is an informal expression in Chinese that roughly translates to "I'm so sorry" or "I'm very sorry." There isn't a single standard English translation for this phrase, as it conveys a sense of deep apology and regret. However, common translations include "I'm terribly sorry," "I apologize deeply," or simply "I'm sorry."
